  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0bc2258f-cebf-42b9-bc8a-493e5f7afae1'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

  <span id="freeText14364045632759719605" style="display:none">Defeated, crushed, and driven almost to extinction, the remnants of the human race are trapped on a planet that is constantly attacked by mysterious alien starfighters. Spensa, a teenage girl living among them, longs to be a pilot. When she discovers the wreckage of an ancient ship, she realizes this dream might be possible—assuming she can repair the ship, navigate flight school, and (perhaps most importantly) persuade the strange machine to help her. Because this ship, uniquely, appears to have a soul.</span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2018-releases">2018-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=poc-rep-side">poc-rep-side</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=ya-sff">ya-sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2569170185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16510053594985792267"><b><em>Skyward</em> felt like a prelude.</b><br/><br/>The raw energy of the closing pages rattles; I started every sentence without knowing where it was going, half-terrified of where it might end. My heart was still pounding from the airy danger of it, even after the turning of the last page. When I looked up, the bedlam of motion inside the coffeeshop where I sat was an underwater warble, and I felt the sort of disorientation you only get when you are pulled out of one world and back into another. That's what any good </span>
  <span id="freeText16510053594985792267" style="display:none"><b><em>Skyward</em> felt like a prelude.</b><br /><br />The raw energy of the closing pages rattles; I started every sentence without knowing where it was going, half-terrified of where it might end. My heart was still pounding from the airy danger of it, even after the turning of the last page. When I looked up, the bedlam of motion inside the coffeeshop where I sat was an underwater warble, and I felt the sort of disorientation you only get when you are pulled out of one world and back into another. That's what any good story does, I suppose.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Is anything fair?” He smiled. </em>
  <br />
  <em>“Death is. He treats us all the same.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />Spensa “Spin” Nightshade was going to be a pilot. As a 7-year-old, she dreamed of it with the raw hope of a child who looked at the stars as if her very soul had unfurled and stretched out to meet it. As a 17-year-old young woman, she knew it with the boundless confidence of a youth who assumed the world will contort itself to accommodate her desires.<br /><br />But Spensa’s name was full of her father’s cowardice in a way nobody could miss. It was a burden and a responsibility. For ten years, Spensa had tried to piece together a father who was gone from rumors that spoke of him deserting his team, of betraying his people. They spewed at her. They poured at her. But when it is all boiled away, what is always left is that wanting, hard and spare and alive: to prove herself, to clear her father’s name, and to fight for humanity’s survival.<br /><br />Even if that meant breaking the rules, leaving them smashed and glittering in her wake.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Remember, Spensa. You get to choose who you are. Legacy, memories of the past, can serve us well. But we cannot let them define us. When heritage becomes a box instead of an inspiration, it has gone too far.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />The novel, the first in Branderson’s latest series, soared through the autumn and winter of 2018 on a frenzy of love, drawing a cornucopia of rave reviews and dominating bestseller lists. And I have to say—it is well-deserved.<br /><br />Clocking in at more than 500 pages, the novel requires patience as it unfolds in slow but ultimately satisfying layers. The meticulous plotting comes off as the work of someone in absolute charge of his craft. The journey may occasionally feel protracted for some, but the latter section is particularly dynamic, full of even more intrigue, adventure and go-for-the-throat thrills. <em>Skyward </em>brims with details that build out into a vast, intricate world which, remarkably, still leaves plenty to explore. It’s a good thing that Sanderson has 4 more books planned for this series as there’s a lot to set up. It’s clear that the author is only getting warmed up; the political and intergalactic machinations that swirled around Spensa had much left to play out. And if Sanderson’s goal was to make his readers clamor for more, I'm pleased to say that he accomplished that goal with flying colors.<br /><br /><em>Skyward</em> is fun, but there’s a deep layer of story at work. Sanderson paints real-world concerns like classism, war profiteering, and patriotic jingoism with piercing resonance. The novel examines, with brilliance and verve, the dangerous culture of martyrdom that is deeply embedded in the DDF—the Defiant Defense Force—and which had, for many years, been preserved in false perfection.<br /><br />Spensa, who recited <em>Defiance</em> like a litany and ripped herself to rags against the sharp and ugly poetry of it, determined to never be called a coward, is confronted with a truth like ice water: the DDF bleeds great gouts of young pilots in the deadly battles against the Krell, but spares the sons and daughters of the elite who are pulled out from the Academy by their wealthy and well-connected parents when the peril becomes too real. Spensa had thought she could join the DDF and vie for the only chance she would ever have at glory, she built her life around that dream, but Spensa soon discovers that her government’s talk of glory and heroism, all their promises, wore a thinner veil than a funeral shroud. Spensa didn’t want to be a part of this machine anymore. But the machine didn’t care. The machine went on grinding and catching her up in its gears.<br /><br />Spensa’s character development doesn’t stop there. All her life the mystery of what had <em>really</em> happened the day her father was unequivocally branded a coward hung over her, and she had hardly dared hope that she might get the answers she longed for like the prize at the end of a long and difficult game. When Spensa does, the truth of it strikes her backhanded, and her heart—for the second time—splits in two and goes to war against itself. The truth—and the sharp certainty of it lodges itself inside Spensa—is never how we want it: clear-cut and shining, a perfect moral center leading us all back home.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Sometimes, the answers we need don’t match the questions we’re asking.” He looked up at me. “And sometimes, the coward makes fools of wiser men.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />That is, I think, what I relished most about this book: the way the author gives his characters plenty of room to fumble and triumph. He made a list of characters that kept getting longer (then, heartbreakingly, shorter) and injected them with enough interiority to keep his readers riveted. Spensa’s journey, in particular, is wonderful to watch, and her potential narrative paths for the sequel are very intriguing.<br /><br />I can’t wait to see where Sanderson takes her.<br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="16510053594985792267" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16724551472557303984"><i>"Just for that, I shall hunt your firstborn and laugh with glee as I tell them of your death in terrible detail, with many unpleasant adjectives!”</i><br/><br/>You know how sometimes you realize you’ve read 500 pages and it was all fluff, nothing really stands out and you can't even remember most of it?<br/><br/> <b>Well this book was the opposite.</b><br/><br/>So much happens, the characters are flawed but their growth is fascinating to watch. The story is complex and becomes more interesting as it progresses. Every time I thought I k</span>
  <span id="freeText16724551472557303984" style="display:none"><i>"Just for that, I shall hunt your firstborn and laugh with glee as I tell them of your death in terrible detail, with many unpleasant adjectives!”</i><br /><br />You know how sometimes you realize you’ve read 500 pages and it was all fluff, nothing really stands out and you can't even remember most of it?<br /><br /> <b>Well this book was the opposite.</b><br /><br />So much happens, the characters are flawed but their growth is fascinating to watch. The story is complex and becomes more interesting as it progresses. Every time I thought I knew where things were going… I was wrong. And happy to be.<br /><br />The teenage angst, an hilarious sentient ship, the lack of romance… This is how you create a fantastic YA book! Sanderson is not afraid to make you laugh... and cry.<br /><br />Absolutely recommend this book.<br /><br />Also shoutout to Doomslug!</span>

  <span id="freeText18325385244929359610" style="display:none">Even though I already had the book, I'm impressed a Brandon Sanderson book was in my November Fairyloot!! Click the link under the picture to see the goods. I think I left out a picture of one of the cards! sigh....<br><br><img alt=" " src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1543014624i/26639873._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2018/11/fairyloot-november-2018-unboxing.html" rel="nofollow noopener">THE GOODS</a><br><br>I had so many things I wanted to say for this review but I have nothing right now! I have cried sad and happy tears. I have loved many. Go read the damn book people! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1541984452ra/26580910.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>It's Brandon Sanderson! What more needs to be said?</b><br><br>Happy Reading! <br><br>Mel 🖤🐶🐺🐾</span>
  <a data-text-id="18325385244929359610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2419655309" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2419655309" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2419655309?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399555770" href="/book/show/39348113-skyward">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2419655309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5318068095010968295"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You get to choose who you are. Legacy, memories of the past, can serve us well. But we cannot let them define us. When heritage becomes a box instead of an inspiration, it has gone too far.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Skyward</i> is the start of a brand-new YA Sci-Fi series by Brandon Sanderson. You all know that I love Brandon Sanderson’s work, especially <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2079341091' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Stormlight Archive</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1466987697' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mistborn</a>, and I knew I couldn’t let this new release pass me by without immediately reading. And, friends, this was nothing short of </span>
  <span id="freeText5318068095010968295" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You get to choose who you are. Legacy, memories of the past, can serve us well. But we cannot let them define us. When heritage becomes a box instead of an inspiration, it has gone too far.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><i>Skyward</i> is the start of a brand-new YA Sci-Fi series by Brandon Sanderson. You all know that I love Brandon Sanderson’s work, especially <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2079341091" rel="nofollow noopener">The Stormlight Archive</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1466987697" rel="nofollow noopener">Mistborn</a>, and I knew I couldn’t let this new release pass me by without immediately reading. And, friends, this was nothing short of a treat. <br /><br />This book follows a young girl named Spensa, who wants nothing more than to follow in her father’s footsteps of being a space pilot and defending her home planet from an alien race called the Krell, who are relentless in their attacking. Unfortunately, her father did something unforgivable and the rest of her community truly will never forget. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“People need stories, child. They bring us hope, and that hope is real.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Spensa lives in future version of our galaxy, on a planet named Detritus. But most of the inhabitants live underground, while only a few cities are above. And in this society people’s job positions are supposed to be based off their test scores that will influence them into learning their strengths, but we soon find out that pilots are mostly found based on their family lineage. <br /><br />Brandon Sanderson really talks about privilege and how outside forces can really impact a person’s life, while a last name can completely make someone’s future. Spensa learns this very quickly, but she is still determined to not only go to flight school, but to graduate at the top of her class, regardless of the people who are willing to do anything to stop her. <br /><br />And Spensa has to go through some really horrible stuff. No spoilers, but even her family is forced to live off of rats, while never being able to see the sky, but living in fear of a lifetime war that never ceases. But Spensa’s determination is awe-inspiring, but she soon realizes that flight school is completely ruthless and very deadly. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It turns out that strange little girls grow up to be strange young women.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Yet, one of the best characters I’ve read all year is easily Spensa. She not only makes you feel immense empathy because of her situation, but just because she’s a little girl that has only known war. She’s passionate, she’s caring, she’s so very dedicated. And she’s hilariously funny. This book made me laugh out loud so many times. But mostly, I was rooting for her from the first to the last page. And she really showcases that everyone has a choice, regardless of the things that life has forced upon them, and regardless of the mistakes of their parents. She was such a wonderful character, and a shining light in 2018’s protagonists. <br /><br />And I loved the constant discussion of what makes a coward and what makes a hero. And about all those grey areas in between those things. And how a different view can really turn those two titles upside down completely. Spensa also meets many new colleagues, some of which who are also chasing the same dream as her, and some who have had it forced upon them. And dare I say, there is a start of an enemies to lovers relationship in this book? Lord, help me. I am already invested! <br /><br />But my heart truly belongs to M-Bot, the AI-driven ship that Spensa finds. A lot of people have compared this book to <i>How To Train Your Dragon</i> and that is so damn accurate, but I actually think I loved M-Bot even more than Toothless. (And that is quite the recommendation, friends!) I also think I just have a soft spot in my heart for sentient ships, if I’m being completely honest. But I have no doubts that if you pick up this book that you will fall in love with M-Bot, too. <br /><br />Okay, so even though I loved this reading experience so much, and I truly think Brandon Sanderson comes up with the best worlds in SFF, two things bothered me about this book. One is a character death, and I won’t go into spoilers, but if you know me at all, you’ll know why this upset me. And Brandon should have done better. Secondly, the ending was a masterpiece. Yeah, you read that right. The ending was magnificent, but it truly overshadowed the rest of the book and made it feel like the 500 pages I just read were some precursor to the actual story that will begin in book two. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Claim the stars, Spensa.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Overall, I did adore this book. It was just what I needed. I actually was feeling really slumpy before I picked this up, and not only did it rectify that, but it reminded me why I love books and stories and fictional worlds so much. I know Brandon Sanderson isn’t for everyone, but he truly is a master at his craft and every book and series he touches turns to gold. And his world-building is honestly on a tier above all else in the genre. And, again, I cannot wait for book two. And I cannot wait to learn everything about a certain blue and orange slug. <br /><br /><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br /><br /><b>Content and trigger warnings</b> for bullying, loss of a loved one, battle scenes, and war themes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5318068095010968295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2222141318" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2222141318" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2222141318?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=brandon-sanderson">brandon-sanderson</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=arc-review-copy">arc-review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=physical-owned">physical-owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2222141318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer656011690955279463"><b>Skyward comes out in mass market paperback today!</b> <br/><br/><i>ARC provided by the publisher, Gollancz, in exchange for an honest review.</i>.<br/><br/><b>4.5 stars.</b><br/><br/><b>Skyward is a fine example of a Young Adult novel.   Once again, I'm in awe of Sanderson who shows he is still at the top of his game.</b> <br/><br/>This novel is another hallmark of Sanderson's ability to spin the most incredible stories. He described the book as How to Train Your Dragon meets Top Gun and Enders Game. These references, however, would count for nothing if the e</span>
  <span id="freeText656011690955279463" style="display:none"><b>Skyward comes out in mass market paperback today!</b> <br /><br /><i>ARC provided by the publisher, Gollancz, in exchange for an honest review.</i>.<br /><br /><b>4.5 stars.</b><br /><br /><b>Skyward is a fine example of a Young Adult novel.   Once again, I'm in awe of Sanderson who shows he is still at the top of his game.</b> <br /><br />This novel is another hallmark of Sanderson's ability to spin the most incredible stories. He described the book as How to Train Your Dragon meets Top Gun and Enders Game. These references, however, would count for nothing if the execution was poor. Fortunately, and to solidify my unwavering faith in my favourite author, he excelled in his first full-length space opera novel. <br /><br />So what do we get from Skyward? Fascinating worldbuilding - check. Empathetic characterisation - check. Excellent pacing and plotting - check. All these I have come to expect from Sanderson already, but the one thing that impressed me the most are the starship dogfight scenes. No magic system to showcase in action? No sweat! He relied on his (seemingly inexhaustible) imagination to create some unique dogfighting techniques while keeping flight science as real as possible with the help and advice of real-life fighter pilots. <br /><br />Similar to his magic systems, the capability of the pilots and their starfighters is constrained within a set of boundaries or rules as dictated by available technology; some of which are made-up to make it more exciting. The flight school arc is engaging and well-written with loads of flight action scenes, and they are so vivid and thrilling that I was practically glued to the pages.<br /> <br />If it is even possible, Sanderson is getting better at his worldbuilding skills, and I'm not just talking about how fascinating this most aptly named planet of Detritus is. It is that self-described Grand Skill of incorporating worldbuilding naturally through the perspective of the characters. Aside from avoiding info-dumping, this also lends an air of mystery to the history of the planet, its inhabitants and their lifelong war, but at the same time is not too obscure as to frustrate the reader.<br /> <br />The story is written mainly in the first-person POV of Spensa - an angry young lady with a lot to prove and hence had quite an attitude problem and a propensity to act like an idiot sometimes. Her growth in character was simply quite superb. While I was annoyed with some of her thoughts and actions at first, she was relatable, and as she fought so hard to remain in flight school at all costs to prove her detractors wrong, the life lessons she faced made her development feel completely natural and realistic. <br /><br />Even the supporting characters are excellent and ones that you will root for and develop an emotional investment. The level of empathy that Sanderson demonstrated in the way he wrote his characters truly astounds me sometimes. My favourite character - who made me tear up and then laugh till I almost cried again - is one that is not even human or biologically alive, but has such a personality as to appear quite sentient.<br /><br />As with all of Sanderson's stories, there are always important themes imbued into the character's journey. Living in the shadow of her father, Spensa went all out to prove that she is not a coward. As she progressed through flight school, however, her conviction of what real bravery is was sorely tested. Her path to be a pilot and a grown-up was one of harsh realities and self-realisation. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>"It has always seemed to me that a coward is a person who cares more about what people say than about what is right. Bravery isn't about what people call you, Spensa. It's about who you know yourself to be."</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br />There is also one unifying theme evident in Sanderson's books, and that is one of hope. Not hope in the metaphysical sense or some god-like intervention, but hope that arises from the good in people. I live for stories like these, especially during these dark and nonsensical times. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>"People need stories, child. They bring us hope, and that hope is real. If that's the case, what does it matter whether people in them actually lived?" </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br />No, it does not matter to me if Kaladin or Dalinar, Vin or Kelsier, (to name a few) are fictional. Their stories illuminate what it means to hope, to live and be human. And I will want to ‘live' those stories again and again. Now, I am adding Spensa and her awesome, hilarious starship into that list.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>You can order this book from: <u><a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/Skyward-Brandon-Sanderson/9781473217874/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u></b>
</i><br /><br /><i>You can also find <a href="http://novelnotions.net/2019/01/06/skyward-skyward-1" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> and my other reviews at <a href="http://novelnotions.net/category/book-reviews/tss-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions.</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="656011690955279463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2571843898" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2571843898" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2571843898?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2571843898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6237172730434688349"><u>2000 hrs., Alta Base, Flight Command Headquarters</u> <br/><br/><b>Scholar:</b> Flight Command, this is Booknerd Twelve, name Katerina. Callsign: Scholar.<br/><b>Flight Command:</b> What are you doing in the outer space, Scholar? Your mission is accomplished, you finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36642458.Skyward__Skyward___1_' title='Skyward (Skyward, #1) by Brandon Sanderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Skyward</a>. Return to the base immediately.<br/><b>Scholar:</b> I’m not ready to leave, Command. <br/><b>Flight Command:</b> Why do you defy direct orders soldier? <br/><b>Scholar:</b> Because there was something about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36642458.Skyward__Skyward___1_' title='Skyward (Skyward, #1) by Brandon Sanderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Skyward</a>; the <b>cinematic quality, the non-stop adventure, the humor and sarcasm, t</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6237172730434688349" style="display:none"><u>2000 hrs., Alta Base, Flight Command Headquarters</u> <br /><br /><b>Scholar:</b> Flight Command, this is Booknerd Twelve, name Katerina. Callsign: Scholar.<br /><b>Flight Command:</b> What are you doing in the outer space, Scholar? Your mission is accomplished, you finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36642458.Skyward__Skyward___1_" title="Skyward (Skyward, #1) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Skyward</a>. Return to the base immediately.<br /><b>Scholar:</b> I’m not ready to leave, Command. <br /><b>Flight Command:</b> Why do you defy direct orders soldier? <br /><b>Scholar:</b> Because there was something about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36642458.Skyward__Skyward___1_" title="Skyward (Skyward, #1) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Skyward</a>; the <b>cinematic quality, the non-stop adventure, the humor and sarcasm, the wonderful crew and the heroine oozing bravado and determination</b>, that won’t let me return. I need more time, to float in space, to soar the winds, to <b>claim the stars</b>, to let the fact that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson" title="Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Brandon Sanderson</a> is a master storyteller not only when he composes the most epic fantasy books ever written, but also the most <b>solid, gripping and awe-inspiring YA science fiction</b> sink in.<br /><b>Flight Command:</b> Why was it such a surprise, Scholar?<br /><b>Scholar:</b> Because the truth is, I was mad at him for engaging with a new YA project that delayed the release of Wax and Wayne #4 and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17250966.Rhythm_of_War__The_Stormlight_Archive___4_" title="Rhythm of War (The Stormlight Archive, #4) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Rhythm of War</a>. But as soon as I took off with Spensa, as soon as I became a part of Skyward Flight, I regretted my anger and all the reservations that held me back. It was truly <b>magnificent</b>, another proof that Brandon Sanderson is <b>the best author of his generation</b>.<br /><b>Flight Command:</b> I understand all these, Scholar, but you have to return. Daydreaming in the outer space is a dangerous (and forbidden) habit. <br /><b>Scholar:</b> But sir, I have my own protectors! <br /><b>Flight Command:</b> Who?<br /><b>Scholar:</b> Doomslug the Destroyer, the most terrifying beast that feasts on the flesh of her enem-<br /><b>Flight Command:</b> That’s simply the cutest slug that ever existed, a soft cupcake.<br /><b>Scholar:</b> Well, there is also the Massacrebot, the most advanced spaceship that will hunt down the first born of his foes and-<br /><b>Flight Command:</b> You know he likes being called M-Bot. And he is not vicious, just a slightly insane talking spaceship that may or may not be the <b>king of sass</b>.<br /><b>Scholar:</b> Fine, there is also the fiercest warrior, Spensa Nightshade, callsign: Spin, the one who bathes in blood and drinks in her cup made of skulls and-<br /><b>Flight Command:</b> Spensa tends to get carried away, and being overly dramatic, but I do recognize that she is one of the bravest, strongest (and funniest) YA heroines out there. Before you start analyzing the might of Skyward cadets and Cobb, the journey to find the meaning of courage and camaraderie, I must confess that while you composed paeans about the glory of Skyward, we launched Reality missiles that will destroy your wings. <br /><b>Scholar:</b> No no no leave my wings alone, I’m setting the coordinates to return, just give me- <br /><br /><i>beep beep beep</i><br /><br /><b>Booknerd Eleven:</b> Sir, was that really necessary?<br /><b>Flight Command:</b> She must learn to control her frenzy every time she reads a book written by Brandon Sanderson. Flight Command out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6237172730434688349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2587860276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2587860276" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2587860276?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2018-shelf">2018-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2587860276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11098191297960416834">Okay, it's official, folks. Brandon Sanderson is a god.<br/><br/>He's not just a go-to guy for all things fantasy. I've read a few of his Cosmere SF stores but this is the first outright SF novel I've read from him and OMG he slams it out of the park. Or sky. :)<br/><br/>Let's put it this way. You remember how <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16278318.Armada' title='Armada by Ernest Cline' rel='nofollow noopener'>Armada</a> should have been the glorious Last Starfighter? Let's just ignore that for a moment.<br/><br/>THIS is the quintessential Top Gun meets the Last Starfighter, complete with a girl pilot with a huge chip on her sho</span>
  <span id="freeText11098191297960416834" style="display:none">Okay, it's official, folks. Brandon Sanderson is a god.<br /><br />He's not just a go-to guy for all things fantasy. I've read a few of his Cosmere SF stores but this is the first outright SF novel I've read from him and OMG he slams it out of the park. Or sky. :)<br /><br />Let's put it this way. You remember how <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16278318.Armada" title="Armada by Ernest Cline" rel="nofollow noopener">Armada</a> should have been the glorious Last Starfighter? Let's just ignore that for a moment.<br /><br />THIS is the quintessential Top Gun meets the Last Starfighter, complete with a girl pilot with a huge chip on her shoulder, a lot of growth to be had, a mysterious AI starship she's caring for while undergoing training, and KILLER dogfights.<br /><br />Did I cry a little as the cadets started dying or being pulled from the classes by freaked out parents? Yes. Did I feel the urgency and the hopelessness and the absolute need for pilots at all costs? Yes. <br /><br />Did I have an INSANE amount of fun reading this?<br /><br />YES.<br /><br /><br />Hell, I'm already devoted to this man's fantasy. <br /><br />I just never guessed, although I SHOULD HAVE GUESSED, that Sanderson's Law was always a great means to bring understandable science-like laws to the field of Fantasy, but COME ON... a man who does this already has a FANTASTIC grip on SF. The story is fantastic, fun, and jammed with action, pathos, and a LOT of cute. :)<br /><br />I can't wait for the next one! It's a great blow out and an even better set-up! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11098191297960416834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3277934421" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17136468179724333053"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36642458.Skyward__Skyward___1_' title='Skyward (Skyward, #1) by Brandon Sanderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Skyward</a><b>(Skyward,#1)</b> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson' title='Brandon Sanderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Brandon Sanderson</a><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1555448218ra/27372868.gif' width='480' height='448' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Skyward was brilliantly written. And it had a compelling, captivating, and engaging storyline. Loved those unique characters. It was a fine read and it wasn’t a bad one by any means, but compared to the other books I’ve read from Brandon Sanderson, it’s by far my least favorite.<br/><blockquote>
  <i>And the warrior’s way was not to run from failure, but to own up to it and do better.</i>
</blockquote><br/><i>Not bad.</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17136468179724333053" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36642458.Skyward__Skyward___1_" title="Skyward (Skyward, #1) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Skyward</a><b>(Skyward,#1)</b> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson" title="Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Brandon Sanderson</a><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1555448218ra/27372868.gif" width="480" height="448" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Skyward was brilliantly written. And it had a compelling, captivating, and engaging storyline. Loved those unique characters. It was a fine read and it wasn’t a bad one by any means, but compared to the other books I’ve read from Brandon Sanderson, it’s by far my least favorite.<br><blockquote>
  <i>And the warrior’s way was not to run from failure, but to own up to it and do better.</i>
</blockquote><br><i>Not bad.</i></span>

<div id="review_3063756046" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3063756046" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3063756046?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3063756046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2481062057163996206">Good news to the die-hard Mistborn fans like me and also The Stormlight Archive lovers (Seriously, I should stop procrastinating and start reading ASAP! It waits too long at my TBR purgatory!), we got the brand new, unique, exciting sci-fi series we’d dreamt of for so long. I honestly waited for second book’s release to start this journey and it finally came out.<br/><br/> The book started a little slow and it gave me idea that was long prologue before taking our first steps into journey and warms us befo</span>
  <span id="freeText2481062057163996206" style="display:none">Good news to the die-hard Mistborn fans like me and also The Stormlight Archive lovers (Seriously, I should stop procrastinating and start reading ASAP! It waits too long at my TBR purgatory!), we got the brand new, unique, exciting sci-fi series we’d dreamt of for so long. I honestly waited for second book’s release to start this journey and it finally came out.<br /><br /> The book started a little slow and it gave me idea that was long prologue before taking our first steps into journey and warms us before the real action starts. We’re introduced the characters and main purpose, the obstacles, enemies, facts and after this long introduction we’re all set to buckle up and move to the space, travelling around the stars and learn more what’s gonna happen. <br /><br />So before reading this book, you may consider this one as a long intro to main story but it is really good written with its perfectly rounded characters and world building. It may be long but don’t give up because especially the cliffhanger shakes you to the core and thrills you so much, makes you want to get the second book into your hands ASAP!<br /><br />Let’s get a quick look to the story progression:<br />Our heroine Spensa Nightshade’s father died a few years ago at the war against the alien race named Krell. Now she wants to be a pilot to honor her father’s memory and defend her planet by fighting against the Krell and avenge her father’s death. But later we learn her father made an unforgiveable mistake and now rest of the colony are so adamant not to forget it. He was accused of being a coward! His wrong move labeled and ruined his own daughter life and after 9 years passed from his demise, Spensa still suffers from his wrong choice’s consequences.<br /><br />But Spensa is fiery, stubborn, powerful, rebellious soul and she is so determined to be trained as a starship pilot and prove her competence. But it’s not gonna be more compelling challenging for her to be accepted to the Defiant Defense Force’s flight school because so many influential and powerful people are against to give her chance get her approval.<br /><br />But with the help of her determination, working her ass off and a little bit luck, she finally finds an empty spot for her to join the program. But her problem doesn’t end so easily. She turns into persona non grata, gets rejected to use the dorms, even the school cafeteria is forbidden zone. She finds herself at a house in cave to stay and she meets with an old, decapitated starfighter named “M-Bot”<br />So as she resumes attending her classes so she also tries to fix this old starfighter. But before without completing her training, she and her classmates find themselves fight against the Krell.<br /><br />Overall, two things really affected me so much about this book. One: I LOVE M-BOT so so so much! I wish I had it in my house and start a starship book club with it!<br /><br />I’m absolutely sure it stole all the show! And the second is (my mouth is till zipped) I’m devastated, so sorry about one of the character’s fortune at this book. (the readers know who I’m talking about and I found it not fair! I even thought to cut one star from my rating but my love for M-Bot and my adoration for the story stopped me.)<br /><br />Brandon Sanderson is uniquely gifted author with his intelligent, visionary brain, he creates remarkable novels. I’m delightfully to read anything his hand touched and worked on.<br /><br />So I cannot wait to start the series’ second book! It’s so much worth to wait for!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2481062057163996206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2588526628" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2588526628" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2588526628?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=ya-science-fiction">ya-science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=military">military</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2588526628&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2588526628" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10329524295227021040">It's a Star Wars training academy sort of story, set on a prison planet surrounded by alien guards.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543879231ra/26683153.gif' width='400' height='169' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Final review, first posted on <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/skyward/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>:<br/><br/>Brandon Sanderson’s new young adult science fiction novel, <i>Skyward</i>, replaces his intricately detailed fantasy magical systems with equally detailed dogfights between one-person starship fighters of the humans living on the planet Detritus (it’s as bleak as it sounds) and the starships of the alien Krell. The Krell chased a fleet of human spaceships t</span>
  <span id="freeText10329524295227021040" style="display:none">It's a Star Wars training academy sort of story, set on a prison planet surrounded by alien guards.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543879231ra/26683153.gif" width="400" height="169" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Final review, first posted on <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/skyward/" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>:<br><br>Brandon Sanderson’s new young adult science fiction novel, <i>Skyward</i>, replaces his intricately detailed fantasy magical systems with equally detailed dogfights between one-person starship fighters of the humans living on the planet Detritus (it’s as bleak as it sounds) and the starships of the alien Krell. The Krell chased a fleet of human spaceships to Detritus decades ago and have pinned them down on the planet since, frequently bombarding the humans with attacks that threaten to wipe out the colony, where people primarily live underground for safety. <br><br>Spensa Nightshade’s father died years ago during a major battle against the Krell. Though other families of spaceship pilots are lauded by the colony, “Chaser” Nightshade was accused of being a coward, fleeing the Krell forces and being shot down and killed by his own flight in retribution, and as an example to others. That cowardice label has lasted through the nine years since his death, continuing to haunt his family and his daughter, Spensa. As a result, at age eighteen she’s a rebellious hothead with a huge chip on her shoulder, and a fiery determination to win a place to be trained as a starship pilot and prove herself as the bravest fighter, ever. Defiant isn’t just a description of the human’s military forces to Spensa; it’s deeply ingrained in her nature.<br><br>Unfortunately for Spensa, there are influential people who are equally determined to see that she does not get a chance to join the Defiant Defense Force’s flight school or graduate as a pilot, convinced that the “defect” in her father is also in the daughter. When she manages to land one of the few spots in the program ― barely, through a combination of hard study, stubbornness and luck ― her troubles aren’t over, by a long shot. Denied the right to live in the school’s dorms or even use the cafeteria, Spensa sets up house in a cave where during a previous excursion she had found a very old, damaged starfighter with (it turns out) a very quirky AI named M-Bot.<br><br>Spensa divides her time between her pilot training classes and trying her hand at secretly repairing the old Starfighter. But the Krell are gradually decimating the human starfighter forces, and Spensa and her classmates are thrown into action against the Krell far sooner than they are ready to handle it.<br><br>After a slightly weak beginning ― Spensa’s brash character and simmering anger got old for me, fast, though I had to admire her sheer determination and refusal to ever give up ― <i>Skyward</i> gains traction and briskly works its way up to an impressive finish. Most of the time in between is spent with training in the semi-military space pilot school for Spensa and her group of ten eighteen-year-old classmates, and with frequent individual spacecraft battles with the Krell aliens. If that sort of story sounds appealing, <i>Skyward</i> should be just the ticket. Though the main emphasis is on action, <i>Skyward</i> also includes some deeper insights into character, and has some excellent points to make about what truly constitutes bravery and cowardice.<br><br>A solid dose of humor is provided by an odd cave creature that Spensa adopts as a mascot of sorts, delightfully naming it Doomslug, and by the personable AI M-Bot.<blockquote>“Not that I require affirmation of any sort, as my emotions are mere simulations … but you are listening to me, right?”<br><br>“I’m listening,” I said. “I’m just thinking.”<br><br>“That is good. I should not like to be maintained by one who lacks brain functions.”</blockquote>The characters in Skyward are, for the most part, familiar types, but they’re still engaging, not to mention quite diverse in their internal and external makeups. Not just Spensa but several of her classmates grow and change significantly through their experiences. The plot is enjoyable, if somewhat predictable, but a few twists toward the end shed a surprising new light on several characters, as well as the ongoing wars with the Krell.<br><br>The ending of <i>Skyward</i> is open-ended, since this is the first book in Sanderson’s new SKYWARD series, but the main plot threads reach a reasonable stopping ― or at least pausing ― point, while leaving me anxious to see where the series goes next. And the sequel is almost here!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10329524295227021040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3330351490" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3330351490" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3330351490?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Battlestar Galactica fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=reviewed-for-fantasy-book-review">reviewed-for-fantasy-book-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=y-a">y-a</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3330351490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer726385757737253875"><b>
  <u><i>Skyward</i> is the freshest and most exciting science-fiction novel I have read in a very long time.</u>
</b><br/><br/>There is a great deal to talk about here because there is a great deal Brandon Sanderson does right. Well, he does everything right really. I do not have a single criticism. The plot is fantastic. The world building is totally excellent. And, as ever, Sanderson gives little away at the start. He slowly builds the layers through the plot and reveals how extensive this world is towards the end. The </span>
  <span id="freeText726385757737253875" style="display:none"><b>
  <u><i>Skyward</i> is the freshest and most exciting science-fiction novel I have read in a very long time.</u>
</b><br /><br />There is a great deal to talk about here because there is a great deal Brandon Sanderson does right. Well, he does everything right really. I do not have a single criticism. The plot is fantastic. The world building is totally excellent. And, as ever, Sanderson gives little away at the start. He slowly builds the layers through the plot and reveals how extensive this world is towards the end. The small little universe the characters have been occupying is part of a much greater expanse. <br /><br />So, this felt like a beginning to a much larger story that has epic potential. Another reviewer called it a prelude, and I am inclined to agree. Sanderson is clever with his storytelling; he always has been. He likes to create illusions for his readers. He likes to make you imagine a world from a certain perspective and then reveal the truth of the situation as time goes on. His stories will never follow the linear path he makes you believe they are going down. And, for me, that’s his greatest strength as a writer. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“People need stories, child. They bring us hope, and that hope is real. If that's the case, what does it matter whether people in them actually lived?”</i>
</b><br /><br />I love this quote. And this story is full of little gems like this one. Central to it all is a remarkably strong young woman who drove the story forward with her unmatched desire to become a pilot, protect her home and see the stars. She is funny and she is weirdly cool. She grew up on stories of epic adventure and has imagined herself the heroine of her own quest, a quest to prove that her father was not a coward and a traitor. She does not want to be branded with such a false legacy. <br /><br />And, as I said before, the story would never quite go in the direction is appeared to be going in. The reveals behind her legacy are feats of storytelling prowess. The seemingly ordinary (yet still engaging) novel about fighter pilots develops into an imaginative and mystical exploration of the human soul and its connection with space and the stars. Although technically young adult, Sanderson captures the stark beauty of human ingenuity here and its will to overcome the most insane odds through nothing but perseverance. There are many adult themes here and some of them quite dark too. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“You get to choose who you are. Legacy, memories of the past, can serve us well. But we cannot let them define us. When heritage becomes a box instead of an inspiration, it has gone too far.”</b>
</i><br /><br />It would be remiss of here not to mention the star-ship, M-bot, the ship with a soul and an obsession with mushrooms. And this idea reminded me of the ships from Robin Hobb’s Liveship Traders series, the idea that a vessel can bond with its owner and together they can achieve extraordinary feats through magic and a telepathic connection. Sanderson only touches on this here as the story comes to a close, though no doubt this will be explored further in the sequels. <br /><br /> Thank you, Brandon Sanderson, for your persistently excellent storytelling. I can genuinely say that it has been over a year since I enjoyed reading a book this much. <br /><br /><b>
  <u><i>Skyward</i> is remarkable in every way, it is so special, and it is easily my favourite Sanderson novel I have read so far. </u>
</b><br /><br />________________________________<br /><br />You can connect with me on social media via <a href="https://linktr.ee/sean.ultra_vegan1" rel="nofollow noopener">My Linktree</a>.<br />__________________________________</span>
  <a data-text-id="726385757737253875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2783400859" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2783400859?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2783400859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7403919238213379690">unpopular opinion, but this story sadly didnt feel like sanderson to me. and that could be for a variety of reasons:<br/><blockquote>- ive only read two other books by him, so i might not know him as an author yet. <br/>- this is my first time reading a YA/sci-fi book of his, so maybe im just not used to it. <br/>- this story feels like plenty of other books i have read before, some of which do this type of story better. </blockquote>and i think its the last point that is really bothering me. even with my limited experience with sande</span>
  <span id="freeText7403919238213379690" style="display:none">unpopular opinion, but this story sadly didnt feel like sanderson to me. and that could be for a variety of reasons:<br /><blockquote>- ive only read two other books by him, so i might not know him as an author yet. <br />- this is my first time reading a YA/sci-fi book of his, so maybe im just not used to it. <br />- this story feels like plenty of other books i have read before, some of which do this type of story better. </blockquote>and i think its the last point that is really bothering me. even with my limited experience with sandersons stories, i can tell that he has such an imagination and really excels at creating new and exciting worlds. but <i>‘skyward’</i> is honestly nothing that i havent read before. and for it to lack that originality and uniqueness i have come to expect from him, its leaving me a little disappointed.<br /><br />there is no doubt this book is a dream for both sanderson and sci-fi fans. there are truly awesome elements to it, but i just couldnt help but feel a bit bored by its predictability. i still love sandersons adult fantasy books, so maybe this genre by him just isnt my favourite. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_2595848022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2595848022" />
    <a title="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader"><img alt="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579173421p2/43850323.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2595848022?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" href="/user/show/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader">Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780525707950" href="/book/show/42654579-skyward">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=breath-in-breath-out">breath-in-breath-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=i-love-the-cover">i-love-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=warm-my-heart">warm-my-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=my-book-bestfriends">my-book-bestfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=original-and-fresh-story">original-and-fresh-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=so-funny-lol">so-funny-lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2595848022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15230679437324930071"><b>THE REVIEW IS POSTED</b> <br/><br/><b>3,7 STARS</b><br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>
<br/>I was a warrior, as Gran-Gran had taught me. And the warrior's way was not to run from failure, but to own up to it and <i>do better</i>.</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>My Opinion Time!</u>
</b><br/><br/>The first time I saw this book, I was captivated by the cover. It was so amazing and it looked eerie and mysterious. After that I also was curious about the book itself because the plot sounded good and something that I would probably love and it's science fiction! one of my favorite genres and I also heard many g</span>
  <span id="freeText15230679437324930071" style="display:none"><b>THE REVIEW IS POSTED</b> <br><br><b>3,7 STARS</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>
<br>I was a warrior, as Gran-Gran had taught me. And the warrior's way was not to run from failure, but to own up to it and <i>do better</i>.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>
  <u>My Opinion Time!</u>
</b><br><br>The first time I saw this book, I was captivated by the cover. It was so amazing and it looked eerie and mysterious. After that I also was curious about the book itself because the plot sounded good and something that I would probably love and it's science fiction! one of my favorite genres and I also heard many great things about it, more reasons for me to read the book! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391453324ra/8390985.gif" width="300" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book was pretty good and it was also funny and action-packed. I love it so much when books manage to make me laugh and I laughed several times while reading this book, a good sign indeed. But I couldn't give it a solid 4 stars or more because while I liked the book, I didn't enjoy it immensely. Like the book could be tedious sometimes. I knew I was bored sometimes, but I kept reading it because the plot of the book was pretty fascinating, even though it could be tedious sometimes but that was not a hindrance for me to keep reading it. To be honest, I initially thought that I wouldn't continue with the series, but I changed my mind and I definitely will read the sequels! even though I didn't love this book, it was still a fun read. <br><br><b>
  <u>The Plot</u>
</b><br><br>The plot was fascinating and I liked it. It was unique and the technology in the book was also cool as well. This book reminded me why I love science fiction very much. But while the plot was fascinating, I also found a problem about it. The pacing of the book was slow and while I didn't complain about it, it could be pretty boring. Things did happen, but still I still found myself quite bored by the book but the plot got better! thankfully. And I my curiosity increased and my heart pounded fast and I felt like I couldn't read it fast enough. The book was action-packed and it was also funny! I laughed and grinned and rolled my eyes several times. I'm so glad I didn't stop reading the book when I was confused in the beginning because the more I read it, the more I understood the story and the technology. I indeed had a pretty good time reading the book. <br><br><b>
  <u>The Characters</u>
</b><br><br>OH MY GOD. I RELLY LOVE DOOMSLUG. She's so cute and Doomslug is a cute creature. She imitated voices and she's just so cute. Every time she spoke I was like " awwwww " damn, I really liked this creature. I should've talked about Spensa or the other characters first but I talked about Doomslug first, so that definitely said something. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550412472ra/27079709.gif" width="350" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And M-Bot! he's also funny and weird. Most of the time, he was the reason I laughed. He's just so unique. And about Spensa, honestly I'm so conflicted every time I think about her. She was incredibly brave, determined and a fierce character. I adored her and I also loved how ambitious and determined she was but there were also times that I just disagreed with the way she way she thought and acted. She could be rude sometimes, but that made her more realistic, I guess. But still, there were times that I just didn't agree with her. <br><br>The friendship in this book was also sweet and heartwarming! I have friends in my real life and I also like them but the friendship in this book was like the other level of the friendship I have in my life. The friendship was heartwarming and strong and I really loved getting to know Spensa's friends! Spensa's really lucky to have them, I wish I had friends like them. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550412741ra/27079716.gif" width="290" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Overall, I liked the book and I had a pretty good time reading it. The book was worth to read.</b><br><br>Thank you very much for reading and liking this review! I appreciate it so much and I hope you all have an amazing day. ❤<br><br> <br>••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••<br><br><b>
  <s> I AM SO EXCITED TO READ THIS BOOK. Science fiction is one of my favorite genres and I've heard great things about this book and I honestly can't wait to meet M-bot and the synopsis also sounds soooo good. Please I'm begging you book do not disappoint me. <br><br>Have you read this book? What did you think of it? (No spoiler please. ☺️)<br></s>
</b></span>
