<div id="review_2629499626" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2629499626" />
    <a title="alana ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12402009-alana"><img alt="alana ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599221603p2/12402009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2629499626?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="alana ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="alana ♡" href="/user/show/12402009-alana">alana ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399555770" href="/book/show/39348113-skyward">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2629499626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4871476861694955671"><b> Rating: 4.5 stars</b><br/><br/><strong>WOW!</strong> This was such an incredibly good book. I am super behind on the Brandon Sanderson train. So behind that this is the first book of his that I've ever read, it definitely will not be the last though. I fell in love with the plot, characters, and world building from the very first page and that almost never happens.<br/><br/><em>Skyward</em> follows a young girl named Spensa (callsign: Spin), who desperately wants to follow in her father's footsteps and become a pilot. In Spensa's world, which </span>
  <span id="freeText4871476861694955671" style="display:none"><b> Rating: 4.5 stars</b><br /><br /><strong>WOW!</strong> This was such an incredibly good book. I am super behind on the Brandon Sanderson train. So behind that this is the first book of his that I've ever read, it definitely will not be the last though. I fell in love with the plot, characters, and world building from the very first page and that almost never happens.<br /><br /><em>Skyward</em> follows a young girl named Spensa (callsign: Spin), who desperately wants to follow in her father's footsteps and become a pilot. In Spensa's world, which takes place in the future, being a pilot is the ultimate honor. However, from the minute this story starts Spensa is constantly put down because her father was deemed a coward and shot down by his co-pilot after betraying his flight crew. Her determination to prove others wrong kept me engaged from the very first page and had me rooting so damn hard for her. Without a doubt Spensa is my favorite character that I read in 2018. She's smart, funny, competitive, so incredibly passionate, and most importantly doesn't take shit from anyone else. She is literally everything I want to be in a person.<br /><br />At first I thought going through flight school might drag the storyline on more than necessary but I was so incredibly wrong. Spensa's fellows classmates all add so much more depth to the story. Their conversations, callsigns, and first few days in the cock pit lead to some pretty hilarious moments, and maybe, kinda, sort of a slow burn romance?!?! Which y'all know my heart and soul is <strong>READY</strong> for it. However, the real star of the story is M-Bot. If you read The Iluminae Files and loved AIDAN then move on over, because theres a new AI ship in town. M-Bot is the softest and sassiest starship I've ever encountered...not that there are many. And if you think I'm not going to love a freaking starship you're dead wrong.<br /><br />While the story sounds all fun it games, it also bring up the conversation of what it means to be a coward <strong>A LOT</strong>. As Spensa continues her pilot training she's realizes that it's not as glorified of a position as she once believed it to be and faces some pretty scary encounters with the enemy ships, called the Krell. It also deals with Spensa digging into her father's past to try and figure out what exactly happened the day he died that made the planet deem him a coward. Which definitely kept me on the edge of my seat trying to guess what happened, and even when I thought I had it figure it out I was still blown away by the ending and in desperate need of the next book. While this book doesn't end on a massive cliffhanger there are still so many unanswered questions that a whole year just seems like a cruel punishment to have to wait.<br /><br /><b>Favorite Quotes</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <br />
  <p>
    <em>“People need stories, child. They bring us hope, and that hope is real. If that's the case, what does it matter whether people in them actually lived?”</em>
  </p>
  <br />
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Sometimes, the answers we need don't match the questions we're asking." He looked up at me. "And sometimes, the coward makes fools of wiser men.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“You have large twin destructor emitters on each wing, along with a light-lance turret underneath. That’s as much firepower as our larger ships. You’re a warship.” </em>
  <br />
  <em>“Clearly not,” M-Bot said. “I’m here to categorize fungi. Didn’t you listen to my last orders? I am not supposed to get into fights.” </em>
  <br />
  <em>“Then why do you have guns?” </em>
  <br />
  <em>“For shooting large and dangerous beasts who might be threatening my fungus specimens,” M-Bot said. “Obviously.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Then [Hurl] sat up, holding out her fist. "Not cowards. No backing down. Brave until the end, right Spin? A pact."</em>
  <br />
  <em>I met her fist with mine. "Brave to the end.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />All in all, I am so glad I was able to buddy read this book with a few of my closest friends here in the book community, Amanda (<a href="https://classyxbookreviews.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Classy x Book Reviews</a>), Ashely (<a href="https://thriftybibliophile.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Thrifty Bibliophile</a>), and <a href="https://booksintheskye.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Books in the Skye.</a> If you're looking for a book with amazing world building, characters, and a plot that will keep you hooked for <strong>DAYS</strong> then don't pass this one up!<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishchicksblog.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookishchick" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishchick_/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4871476861694955671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2618614168" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2618614168" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2618614168?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399555770" href="/book/show/39348113-skyward">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2618614168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11888494272920804725"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488951954ra/22171293.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>“You get to choose who you are. Legacy, memories of the past, can serve us well. But we cannot let them define us. When heritage becomes a box instead of an inspiration, it has gone too far.”</i><br/><br/>Story 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br/>When Spensa was a little girl she always dreamed about flying, seeing the stars, the sky. <br/>Being free, even just for a moment. <br/>Even though there were stones upon her path that nearly let her tumble and get lost, she still found a way to be upon the sky. <br/>To see the stars, the sky and to discover wha</span>
  <span id="freeText11888494272920804725" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488951954ra/22171293.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“You get to choose who you are. Legacy, memories of the past, can serve us well. But we cannot let them define us. When heritage becomes a box instead of an inspiration, it has gone too far.”</i><br><br>Story 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>When Spensa was a little girl she always dreamed about flying, seeing the stars, the sky. <br>Being free, even just for a moment. <br>Even though there were stones upon her path that nearly let her tumble and get lost, she still found a way to be upon the sky. <br>To see the stars, the sky and to discover what happened to her father. What made him run from a fight. <br>First of all, I’m not into sci-fi.<br>I was never a big fan of it. <br>But after reading many reviews that told me that this book was awesome and that it had such a well balanced fast pacing, I was 💯 going to at least try it out. <br>And what can I say? It wasn’t perfect, no by all means it’s nearly impossible for a book to be perfect, but it was good. <br>It was really really good. <br>And I enjoyed every minute of it. <br><br>Btw. This was one of the best Buddy reads I had in a while. It was so much fan talking to one of my favorite persons on this platform. <br>So thank you, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/58818027-fares" rel="nofollow noopener">Fares</a>, for making this BR so funny and making me smile a lot ☺️<br><br>Character 🌟🌟🌟🌟<br><i>“So . . . ," I said. "You're saying that by the end of our training, you expect us to be able to use grappling hooks made of energy to smash our enemies with flaming chunks of space debris?"<br>"Yes."<br>"That . . . ," I whispered, "that's the most beautiful thing I've ever heard.” </i><br>I like confident characters. <br>As long as they don’t overdo it. <br>I know Spensa is a little bit over the top. But sometimes she felt so real. <br>Thinking she will be the best pilot on her team, but then crashing a lot of times and taking a lot of time to learn things. <br>She thought the sky, the fights, everything was like it should’ve been in her dreams. <br>But then she fell, she lost and she grieved. <br>She saw the dangerous part of the sky, but she never bolted. She saw that there was danger to a lot of things, including for her being a pilot. But she never wavered. <br>Even though people told her she should stay on ground, she should give up, give up, give up. <br>She never did. <br>She never gave up. <br>And even though she had a time we’re she overthought thinks, where she had insecurities, she soon realized that you can’t be afraid of a thing you don’t know for certain. <br>All in all I fell absolutely in love with her. <br>I know she had her flaws, but who is perfect, huh? <br>My favorite character was probably M-Bot. He was be cutest, funniest and weirdest thing I have read about in a long time.<br>He kind of reminded me of Aidan, but In a cute innocent cinnamon roll way. <br>He made the most random announcement and statements and every time he appeared I was happy and smiling. <br>I loved him so much, even though he was an AI. <br>Then there was Jorgen, our flight leader and Jerkface. Even though I hated him in the beginning, i knew I would love him in the end. <br>(I can sometimes feel this kind of stuff.)<br>And what can I say? I was totally right. <br>I loved him. He was such a talented and brilliant flight leader. <br>Then there was Spins best friend and another really talented and smart boy, Rig. <br>What I loved most about him was his kind heart. Even though everyone hated Spensa and was super mean to her, he was her only and her best friend. <br>He also was super talented in a lot of things, shy but also really lovable guy. <br>All in all I can say that I loved all the main and side characters. ♥️<br><br>World 🌟🌟🌟<br>There was a war in the sky - many many years ago. The humans were attacked by aliens, they later called them Krell. <br>The humans landed on a planet, scattered around in small clans. But every time they tried to build something, to start a civilization, the Krell came and destroyed it. Many years ago there was a battle - called the battle of Alta. Many pilots fell, many pilots died, but the human race survived and they won. <br>But the war never ended.<br>Like I said, I’m not a fan of sci-fi. That’s why I’m not a professional in it. <br>I don’t know if this book is a brilliant sci-fi book. So I’ll just try to tell you what I think as a not-professional-sci-fi-reader. <br>I think this world isn’t perfect. I don’t think it’s really realistic, that parents let their kids become a pilot, only to see them being shot down. Then when the fight is over, the other pilots are forced to continue like nothing happened. There are many kids - not even eighteen- that train everyday only to be send into a battle and die. <br>There is war everywhere. Kids, little children dream about being a pilot, to fly, to fight against the Krell. <br>I know there is the leader, there are powerful people that control everything, but I thought that there were not enough emotions and reactions from the population. <br>It was so quiet. <br>Also I think it’s really weird that they never really tried to learn more about the Krell. They just fought them every time. Even though they didn’t know what they were and what they wanted. They just fought. <br>I know that sounds stupid and weird, but I thought that was really unrealistic. <br>Also, every other pilot is like: „I follow commands, I never question them.“ and then there are these kids, not even full pilot and they ask the important questions. Uh, yeah. <br>Buuuuuut still I thought the whole idea was great. <br><br>Relationships 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>You know what I really really love in books? Strong friendship. It doesn’t matter if it’s between a boy and a boy, or a girl and a girl or between a girl and a boy. <br>And this book is full of it. There is no romance, even though I wished it had at least a little bit of it, but it was full of friendship, of loyalty, of smart kids and kind and brave hearts. <br>I loved that there were teams. And even though they were so different, they still found their way. <br>That was my absolute favorite part. <br>That’s why I give this part a six star! <br>Woohoo! 🥳<br><br>Writing style 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>This was my first Brandon Sanderson book and what can I say? It won’t be the last. <br>He’s such a talented writer. <br>I couldn’t put the book down. <br>If I wouldn’t have a social life and a work place I would’ve finished this in one day. <br>It was so fast paced and full of action, friendship, secrets and intrigues. <br>It was all in all a really really really good book. <br>I loved it so much and I’m glad I tried it out! <br>I can definitely recommend this to everyone that loves some action and friendship.<br><br><i>“People need stories, child. They bring us hope, and that hope is real. If that's the case, what does it matter whether people in them actually lived?" </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11888494272920804725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=books-of-my-heart">books-of-my-heart</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=cool-creatures">cool-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2591720513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16519959721226361670"><b>Audible Daily Deal: 02May19 for 5.95 <a href='https://www.audible.com/pd/Skyward-Audiobook/B07H7Q5D3M?serial=&source_code=AUDOREM0405189NA9>here</a></b> Totally worth that for M-bot and Doomslug<br /><br /><b><a href=' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>This review was originally posted on Books of My Heart</a></b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“That music the water makes,” she said. “Isn’t it the most wonderful sound ever?”<br/>“The most wonderful sound ever is the lamentations of my enemies, screaming my name toward the heavens with ragged, dying voices.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><b>Bless My Stars this was fantastic!</b> You know how you are going along in your life thinking that most of the stuff you are reading is good, and it is, but then you read something and it m</span>
  <span id="freeText16519959721226361670" style="display:none"><b>Audible Daily Deal: 02May19 for 5.95 <a href="https://www.audible.com/pd/Skyward-Audiobook/B07H7Q5D3M?serial=&amp;source_code=AUDOREM0405189NA9&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/b&gt; Totally worth that for M-bot and Doomslug&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;a href=" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">This review was originally posted on Books of My Heart</a></b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“That music the water makes,” she said. “Isn’t it the most wonderful sound ever?”<br />“The most wonderful sound ever is the lamentations of my enemies, screaming my name toward the heavens with ragged, dying voices.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Bless My Stars this was fantastic!</b> You know how you are going along in your life thinking that most of the stuff you are reading is good, and it is, but then you read something and it makes everything else seem dull by comparison. Skyward (most Brandon Sanderson books actually) was like that for me.<br /><br />Let me tell you that this book has absolutely no kissing in it, like none and I still LOVED it. Not liked, but thought if it has more romance it would be better, no I LOVED this book and thought that everything about it was perfect. Sure, I’m hoping long term we are warming up and there will be a romance but SCUD it, I’ll be okay if there isn’t one, you can <b>*gasp*</b> in amazement now.<br /><br /><b>So you probably want to know why this is in my TOP 3 books for 2018 at the moment.</b>:<br /><br />First there is the MC Spensa a.k.a. spin. She is just this wonderfully fun character so full of anger, bravado and temper. Plus she has a great imagination and I love every single time that she tells someone off, it is hilarious and slightly barbaric. She even gets a doomslug for her mascot and finds and incredibly funny talking ship along the way. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Is my father why I’m such a mess of anger, bravado, and temper? Is the fact that they call him a coward the reason I walk around with my sword in hand, screaming that I’ll make a pile of everyone’s skulls, then stand on that to help me behead the people who were too tall for me to reach?”<br />Kimmalyn smiled fondly. <br />“Bless my stars?” I asked her. <br />“Every single one of them, Spensa. Every single bouncing star.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br />Second is the mystery of this world. Why are the humans even fighting the Krell, how come the Krell never field more than 100 ships, what is the truth behind the death of Spensa’s father, what is the history of these people and how they came to this planet, where did M-bot come from etc, etc. Sanderson always does a great job of surprising me and this book had some big surprises in it.<br /><br />Third is the side characters. Spensa’s flight school classmates make up a wide blend of different characters and it is so much fun to watch them go from a disjointed collection of kids to a group of friends and team mates. Alas this is a dangerous place and not all the kids are going to make it to graduation. The danger is real and I felt every second of the suspense in each battle wondering who wouldn’t be coming back. Still I loved getting to know all of them and each brought something special to the story.<br /><br />Fourth is M-bot, I know I mentioned him above (talking ship) but I think that I highlighted almost everything M-bot said in this book. He was hilarious and brought some much-needed comic relief to the story. Truly my favorite side character in the story.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You have large twin destructor emitters on each wing, along with a light-lance turret underneath. That’s as much firepower as our larger ships. You’re a warship.” <br />“Clearly not,” M-Bot said. “I’m here to categorize fungi. Didn’t you listen to my last orders? I am not supposed to get into fights.” <br />“Then why do you have guns?” <br />“For shooting large and dangerous beasts who might be threatening my fungus specimens,” M-Bot said. “Obviously.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />And lastly was the Son of a Supernova ‘Jerkface’ himself. I love when your perceptions of someone can be changed over the course of a story. I pretty much hated him at the beginning but by the end I guess I could say that a ‘ship’ might be in my future for this series. I could definitely get on board a Spensa/Jerkface ship in the long run. <br /><br />I haven’t read a lot of space opera’s but I think that this book has something in it for every fantasy lover and most readers. It was entertaining, emotional and had just about everything I want in a book (I mentioned the no kissing already). I have over 230+ highlights and can’t wait to reread it sometime in the near future, probably right before the next book comes out. So if you didn’t get that I’m very enthusiastic about this book let me say 3 final words. <b>READ THIS NOW!!! </b><br /><br /><b>Audio Note</b> - I have never been disappointed with a narrator for a Sanderson book and the streak still holds. Suzy Jackson was fantastic. She performed this book splendidly and I always knew who was talking. Her portrayal of Spensa was great and M-bot so funny. I haven’t listened to anything she narrated before but I’ll definitely look through her catalogue to see what else I might like. I listened at my normal 1.5x speed. <br /><br /><br /><strong>Listen to a clip:</strong><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://soundcloud.com/orionbooks/skyward-by-brandon-sanderson-read-by-sophie-aldred">https://soundcloud.com/orionbooks/sky...</a><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="16519959721226361670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2253415285" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2253415285" />
    <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner"><img alt="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551272804p2/3481302.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2253415285?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner">Eon ♒Windrunner♒  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2253415285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8752894005945828201"><i>I was lucky enough to be provided an ARC from the publisher, Gollancz, via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review. Thank you so much for giving me the opportunity.</i><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1541143896i/26535882._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='276' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>Rating: 4.5 stars<br/><br/><i>
  <b>Brandon Sanderson shoots for the stars in Skyward, the first entry of his sci-fi adventure, and absolutely aces the takeoff. </b>
</i><br/><br/>Is there anything better than a new book release from your favourite author?<br/><br/>Ok, I have to admit though. I am not a huge fan of sci-fi books, and as such avoid them where possible. I will </span>
  <span id="freeText8752894005945828201" style="display:none"><i>I was lucky enough to be provided an ARC from the publisher, Gollancz, via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review. Thank you so much for giving me the opportunity.</i><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1541143896i/26535882._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="276" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Rating: 4.5 stars<br><br><i>
  <b>Brandon Sanderson shoots for the stars in Skyward, the first entry of his sci-fi adventure, and absolutely aces the takeoff. </b>
</i><br><br>Is there anything better than a new book release from your favourite author?<br><br>Ok, I have to admit though. I am not a huge fan of sci-fi books, and as such avoid them where possible. I will however make exceptions for my favourite authors, and Brandon Sanderson is right at the pinnacle of that list. Still, I had my doubts, this being a space opera.<br><br><i>*gives doubting self a reproving glare in the mirror</i><br><br>This is Brandon Sanderson guys - there is no need to doubt. A few frantic reading sessions later I can excitedly confirm, the master of fantasy, Brandon Sanderson, has brought his particular brand of AWESOMENESS to the sci-fi genre as well.<br><br>Spensa (callsign: Spin) dreams of being a starfighter pilot for the Defiant Defense Force. The DDF’s main objective: To defend the planet Detritus from the Krell, aliens determined to destroy humankind. She has studied for years to make her dream come true and knows every possible answer that she may need to pass the flight school test that ensures admittance to the pilot training program. If fate had dealt her a different hand, she would not even have to write the test, but would receive automatic acceptance into the school on grounds of being the daughter of one of the heroes of the Battle of Alta. Her father (callsign: Chaser) was one of, if not the DDF’s best pilot , when the famous fight took place. During the battle however, he inexplicably lost his nerve and tried to flee the fight to save his own hide and was consequently shot down by his own team to discourage any other pilot from following his example.<br><br>His branding as a coward, and the stigma allotted to his family by association ensured a tough upbringing for Spensa, making her goal of becoming a pilot akin to the punishment of Sisyphus. The deck is stacked against her - there are few who have any respect for the daughter of a craven, and many who do not want her to succeed. She is obstinately determined though to fulfill her destiny - she will pass the flight school test and become one of the best pilots in the fleet, thereby restoring her family name. And then in the middle of her mission to succeed she makes a monumental discovery that could change her life completely, but also change the course for the entire war effort for good...a starship of unknown design with an AI built-in.<br><br>As is the norm with this author, the story is very well written. This might be labeled as YA, but I found my enjoyment at the same level as any of his other works and would ignore the label entirely. Some of my favourite narrative devices are present, in a prologue that skips a number of years forward at the first chapter and a lost history where no-one really knows much about what happened in the past. Pacing is brisk and the Sanderson avalanche is present, although not at a Stormlight Archive intensity in my opinion. It does not take anything away from the gripping ending though and should not dissuade anyone from reading this either. World-building is wonderful once again. Sanderson is just… a genius. Characterization is complex and fun, I loved the protagonist, the growth she exhibits throughout and had an easy time enjoying reading about every major and minor character in Skyward. Especially MBot :)<br><br> <blockquote>“...human beings need someone friendly to listen to them when they’re grieving. So feel free to talk to me. I will be friendly. You have nice shoes.”<br> “Is that the only thing you notice about people?”<br> “I’ve always wanted shoes. They’re the sole piece of clothing that makes any sense, assuming ideal environmental conditions. They don’t play into your strange and nonsensical taboos about not letting anyone see your—”<br> “Is this really the only thing you can think of to comfort someone who is grieving?”<br> “It was number one on my list.” Great.<br> “The list has seven million entries. Do you want to hear number two?”<br> “Is it silence?”<br> “That didn’t even make the list.”<br> “Move it to number two.”<br> “All right, I . . . Oh.”</blockquote><br><br>As for the magic-system... it’s actually non-existent this time. <i>Whaaaaatttt???</i>, I know, I know, but taking its place are all sorts of fascinating rules governing starfighter movement and fighting and as expected Sanderson brings these to life with vivid imagery easily relayed. Lastly, as with many other Sanderson books, this one also features important themes, touching on fulfillment, self-realization and identity. Yup, it’s a Sanderson book through and through, which should make every fan rejoice.<br><br>This one did. <b>Repeatedly.</b><br><br><i>Skyward will be released on November 6th 2018. I loved both the UK cover and US cover for this book, thus the posting of both above and a shout out to the immensely talented <b>Sam Green</b> and <b>Charlie Bowater</b> for your amazing artwork.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8752894005945828201" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4666434437614187292"><b>EDIT:</b> The book dropped a few days ago, everyone needs to go read it ASAP, you won't regret it!!<br/><br/><b>*AS MANY STARS AS THERE ARE DEBRIS IN THE RUBBLE BELT*</b><br/><br/>Okay, let me start off with this: <br/>I <i>live</i> for Spensa. <br/>I <i>adore</i> Spensa. <br/>I <i>look up to</i> Spensa. <br/><br/>Since this book hasn't been officially released yet and I don't want to spoil anything, I'll be keeping this short. What I will say is that I would have given this 5 stars for Spensa alone. But throw a precious, sassy and funny sidekick, a band of awesome and l</span>
  <span id="freeText4666434437614187292" style="display:none"><b>EDIT:</b> The book dropped a few days ago, everyone needs to go read it ASAP, you won't regret it!!<br /><br /><b>*AS MANY STARS AS THERE ARE DEBRIS IN THE RUBBLE BELT*</b><br /><br />Okay, let me start off with this: <br />I <i>live</i> for Spensa. <br />I <i>adore</i> Spensa. <br />I <i>look up to</i> Spensa. <br /><br />Since this book hasn't been officially released yet and I don't want to spoil anything, I'll be keeping this short. What I will say is that I would have given this 5 stars for Spensa alone. But throw a precious, sassy and funny sidekick, a band of awesome and loyal flightmates and some seriously kickass airfights into the mix and we’ve got ourselves a masterpiece!<br /><br />This was my first ever Brandon Sanderson book, and I’m kicking myself for not having picked up any of his other books earlier if they’re all going to be this good! <br />I’m usually not that into sci-fi so I'll probably enjoy his fantasy series even more, <s>which I can't imagine</s>, but hell, this was damn epic and blew me away. His way of telling stories just sucks you right in! I laughed, cried, doubted and mourned with Spensa throughout this whirlwind of an adventure.<br /><br /><i>Received a free copy of this book from the publisher via Netgalley in exchange for my honest review.</i></span>

<div id="review_2586470547" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2586470547" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2586470547?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2586470547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6895103963270433792">I'm definitely pleased that Sanderson is back to writing books I adore and surprising me. I certainly wasn't sure if the fantasy author I've read previously would be able to turn his hand so effectively to Sci fi but I am pleased to confirm he did it again.<br/><br/>This is the story of a human race who are clinging onto existence whilst under fire from an alien race called the Krell. Humans have fled Earth in ships many years ago, and they are conducting a kind of last stand battle with the Krell to be a</span>
  <span id="freeText6895103963270433792" style="display:none">I'm definitely pleased that Sanderson is back to writing books I adore and surprising me. I certainly wasn't sure if the fantasy author I've read previously would be able to turn his hand so effectively to Sci fi but I am pleased to confirm he did it again.<br /><br />This is the story of a human race who are clinging onto existence whilst under fire from an alien race called the Krell. Humans have fled Earth in ships many years ago, and they are conducting a kind of last stand battle with the Krell to be able to survive and keep on going. They are continually bombarded and have to train up their young children to aspire to become Pilots, and they have a lot of battle instinct that has been carried through from past Earth days, but much of their technology has been lost. <br /><br />The main character is Spensa, a young girl who is about to try and take her Pilot's test, but there is a problem. Spensa's father has been branded by all as a traitor and a coward it seems that in this society the crimes of the parent are passed on to the child and family. Spensa and her mother and gran have gone from the family of an esteemed pilot to the outcasts and she has a hard time making friends and being allowed basic human courtesies.<br /><br />Some of the things I most enjoyed about this were the way that the fight scenes (something I almost always dislike) actually felt really immediate and fun. The way Sanderson writes his battles is always good, and that's true again in this story where you feel involved in the chaos being wrought by the Krell. <br /><br />I have to say, I am also impressed by the characters in this book as there were a lot of them to enjoy and many of them felt very well developed and fleshed out. We have Spensa as our main character of course, she is feisty and silly and she has a hard exterior after all the taunts she has had to put up with. She's a bit of a dreamer and she loves being in the action and shouting about how she will destroy people, but she's also logical and clever and she is a great PoV to follow.<br />Next I loved M-Bot who is a sentient ship we meet later on. I don't want to tell you too much more about this character, but suffice to say they are pretty sarcastic, silly, judgemental in a fun way, and mushroom-obsessed :D.<br />Rig was also a character I liked a lot because he's a brainiac and a nerdy friend and he's exactly the kind of stereotype I love to love. He's funny and too clever by a mile, but he's also super caring for his friends and he and Spensa work well together.<br />We have Cogg who is a flight instructor, Jurgen (aka Jerkface) and Kimmalyn too, all of whom I enjoyed getting to know and I feel like they all played a good part in Spensa's story. I like seeing how they all interacted with her and helped her with things she wasn't sure about, and I think that they made a great team!<br />Finally, we have a blue and orange slug found in a cave called Doomslug, and that is the best name ever :D<br /><br />The plot was fast moving for this one and I never found myself bored, in fact I wasn't to uncover the mystery of Spensa's father as much as she did. I definitely think Sanderson has managed to write a book that is pretty lengthy, but it feels very easy to read once again and I whizzed through it enjoying learning about the life the humans lead and the battles they fight daily.<br /><br />On the whole, a very dramatic story with a lot of happy and sad moments and a few surprises too. It's not my favourite Sanderson, but it's exactly the right kind of read to lift you up and make you enjoy the story, and I think that it's a great way to break up some of the fantasy reading I have recently been doing. 4.5*s from me and recommended :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="6895103963270433792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2589011972" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2589011972" />
    <a title="Dana Ilie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21690081-dana-ilie"><img alt="Dana Ilie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584606424p2/21690081.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2589011972?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Ilie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Ilie" href="/user/show/21690081-dana-ilie">Dana Ilie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/39353738-skyward">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21690081-dana-ilie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2589011972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13992222546254040085">Sanderson’s world-building is one of the most interesting aspects to the story. He ekes out information at a steady rate as to not overwhelm the reader with massive info dumps and maintains an air of mystery as to how the circumstances of Spin’s people came to be. Skyward has all the hallmarks of a Sanderson story: mysterious prologue, likeable protagonists, curious past civilizations, new technologies, and the looming threat of a warring race. I was often reminded of Mistborn’s ‘metal burning’ </span>
  <span id="freeText13992222546254040085" style="display:none">Sanderson’s world-building is one of the most interesting aspects to the story. He ekes out information at a steady rate as to not overwhelm the reader with massive info dumps and maintains an air of mystery as to how the circumstances of Spin’s people came to be. Skyward has all the hallmarks of a Sanderson story: mysterious prologue, likeable protagonists, curious past civilizations, new technologies, and the looming threat of a warring race. I was often reminded of Mistborn’s ‘metal burning’ magic when Skyward’s new tech abilities were showcased. Sanderson has created a system of rules for a ship’s dogfighting technology, then immediately dives into all the various strategies of how to best employ it, pushing its capabilities ever further and testing the boundaries of how far this tech can function. It’s always a pleasure spending time inside Brandon’s mind as he creates a new playground of rules and takes his characters for a ride through unchartered territories.<br /><br />I won’t say much about him, but I LOVED M-Bot. He’s such an interesting character and honest to god funny. I kept laughing throughout his dialogue, and his obsession with mushrooms cracked me up all the time. That’s all I’m saying! Just trust my vague assurances that you’ll love him.<br /><br />In addition to some of the themes discussed above, this story also explores the nature of identity, both human and artificial. Identity can be defined by how some human characters act and think, but this also applies to an AI struggling to determine whether it can create new ideas on its own. Following these character arcs helped ground the story between tense scenes of battle training and hidden agendas, and I appreciated how the story sometimes slowed down to concentrate on the consequences of our characters’ decisions. And these consequences are often dire: the violence is hardly graphic, but its repercussions are felt heavily throughout the story.<br />Skyward is an easy book to recommend. It contains all the main characteristics of a Sanderson novel from a writer at the top of his game. Some might consider this book YA, though I was just as engrossed as I would have been with any other of his novels. Above all, this novel is a ton of fun, and it sets up the story for some excellent ideas to explore in the next volume. Thankfully, we won’t have to wait long, as Brandon has shared that the sequel was just submitted to the publisher. I’ve grown quite fond of the characters in this story and am curious to unravel its mysteries in the series ahead.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13992222546254040085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ashley Nuckles" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55308610-ashley-nuckles"><img alt="Ashley Nuckles" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570249252p2/55308610.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Nuckles" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Nuckles" href="/user/show/55308610-ashley-nuckles">Ashley Nuckles</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3100893643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9761831474169714279">Ok I don’t know where to begin: this was SO. GOOD. At times the description of space travel and flight movements was a bit confusing, but once you got it the story got GOOOOD. I love Spensa and I love the backstory that we learn at the very end because it seems like it could lead into a verrrrry interesting sequel. EXCITED!</span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OkXLN6leT4T0ZrKG6qwAQZ0xAMnDxpSEyo/E2QN9vYNYfkaRiN1qhXHkrb/PJC6LExaxF6zTLbU6Qg3AIiCDzQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('E7arD3V2tGubvYTxzHNiVtc4qCCqaYYeJJq/z/se3kNxjSapVPWRah4/m8jp+0ycWR8Z/sV8Py/UV3bW2kPgDQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson">About Brandon Sanderson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1394044556p3/38550.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson">Brandon Sanderson
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17928191338590979557">Brandon’s major books for the second half of 2016 are <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18714787.The_Dark_Talent' title='The Dark Talent' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dark Talent</a>,</i> the final volume in Alcatraz Smedry’s autobiographical account of his battle against the Evil Librarians who secretly rule our world, and <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28595941.Arcanum_Unbounded' title='Arcanum Unbounded' rel='nofollow noopener'>Arcanum Unbounded</a>,</i> the collection of short fiction in the Cosmere universe that includes the Mistborn series and the Stormlight <br/>Archive, among others. This collection features <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul' title='The Emperor’s Soul' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Emperor’s S</a></i></span>
  <span id="freeText17928191338590979557" style="display:none">Brandon’s major books for the second half of 2016 are <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18714787.The_Dark_Talent" title="The Dark Talent" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark Talent</a>,</i> the final volume in Alcatraz Smedry’s autobiographical account of his battle against the Evil Librarians who secretly rule our world, and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28595941.Arcanum_Unbounded" title="Arcanum Unbounded" rel="nofollow noopener">Arcanum Unbounded</a>,</i> the collection of short fiction in the Cosmere universe that includes the Mistborn series and the Stormlight <br />Archive, among others. This collection features <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul" title="The Emperor’s Soul" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor’s Soul</a>,</i> <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28698036.Mistborn__Secret_History" title="Mistborn: Secret History" rel="nofollow noopener">Mistborn: Secret History</a>,</i> and a brand-new Stormlight Archive novella, <i>Edgedancer</i>.<br /><br />Earlier this year he released <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15704486.Calamity" title="Calamity" rel="nofollow noopener">Calamity</a>,</i> the finale of the #1 New York Times bestselling Reckoners trilogy that began with <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17182126.Steelheart" title="Steelheart" rel="nofollow noopener">Steelheart</a>
</i>.<br /><br />Brandon Sanderson was born in 1975 in Lincoln, Nebraska. As a child Brandon enjoyed reading, but he lost interest in the types of titles often suggested to him, and by junior high he never cracked a book if he could help it. This changed when an eighth grade teacher gave him <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/176268.Dragonsbane" title="Dragonsbane" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonsbane</a>
</i> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10333.Barbara_Hambly" title="Barbara Hambly" rel="nofollow noopener">Barbara Hambly</a>.<br /><br />Brandon was working on his thirteenth novel when Moshe Feder at Tor Books bought the sixth he had written. Tor has published <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68427.Elantris" title="Elantris" rel="nofollow noopener">Elantris</a>,</i> the Mistborn trilogy and its followup <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10803121.The_Alloy_of_Law" title="The Alloy of Law" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law</a>,</i> <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1268479.Warbreaker" title="Warbreaker" rel="nofollow noopener">Warbreaker</a>,</i> and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7235533.The_Way_of_Kings" title="The Way of Kings" rel="nofollow noopener">The Way of Kings</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11543195.Words_of_Radiance" title="Words of Radiance" rel="nofollow noopener">Words of Radiance</a>,</i> the first two in the planned ten-volume series The Stormlight Archive. He was chosen to complete <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6252.Robert_Jordan" title="Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Jordan</a>’s Wheel of Time series; 2009’s <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1166599.The_Gathering_Storm" title="The Gathering Storm" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gathering Storm</a>
</i> and 2010’s <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8253920.Towers_of_Midnight" title="Towers of Midnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Towers of Midnight</a>
</i> were followed by the final book in the series, <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1166599.A_Memory_of_Light" title="A Memory of Light" rel="nofollow noopener">A Memory of Light</a>,</i> in January 2013. Four books in his middle-grade <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/623976.Alcatraz_vs__the_Evil_Librarians" title="Alcatraz vs. the Evil Librarians" rel="nofollow noopener">Alcatraz vs. the Evil Librarians</a>
</i> series have been released in new editions by Starscape, and his novella <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12796771.Infinity_Blade_Awakening" title="Infinity Blade Awakening" rel="nofollow noopener">Infinity Blade Awakening</a>
</i> was an ebook bestseller for Epic Games accompanying their acclaimed <i>Infinity Blade</i> iOS video game series. Two more novellas, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13452375.Legion" title="Legion" rel="nofollow noopener">Legion</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul" title="The Emperor’s Soul" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor’s Soul</a>,</i> were released by Subterranean Press and Tachyon Publications in 2012, and 2013 brought two young adult novels, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10137823.The_Rithmatist" title="The Rithmatist" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rithmatist</a>
</i> from Tor and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17182126.Steelheart" title="Steelheart" rel="nofollow noopener">Steelheart</a>
</i> from Delacorte.<br /><br />The only author to make the short list for the David Gemmell Legend Award six times in four years, Brandon won that award in 2011 for <i>The Way of Kings</i>. <i>The Emperor’s Soul</i> won the 2013 Hugo Award for Best Novella. He has appeared on the <i>New York Times</i> Best-Seller List multiple times, with five novels hitting the #1 spot.<br /><br />Currently living in Utah with his wife and children, Brandon teaches creative writing at Brigham Young University.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17928191338590979557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
